# Script patches — method fills for hollow FO76 scripts

FO76 ships many activator / furniture / fragment scripts with their bodies
**stripped server-side**: the client `.pex` keeps the script's properties and
states but contains no event logic. When the FO76→FO4 conversion decompiles one,
the resulting `.psc` is a logicless skeleton, so the converted object does nothing
in FO4 (a water pump that gives no water, wind chimes you can't take, etc.).

A patch here supplies **only the method/event bodies** you want to inject. The
pipeline decompiles the FO76 script to get its real skeleton (Scriptname,
`Extends`, property list, states), then **splices your members into it**:

During FO76→FO4 decompilation, known source-only script types are adapted
case-insensitively to FO4 types. In particular, `QuestInstance` becomes `Quest`
in `Extends` declarations and scalar/array property types.

- A patch `Function`/`Event` whose name matches a top-level member of the skeleton
  **replaces** that member's body.
- A patch member with no match is **appended** into the script's default state.
- Members placed inside a patch `State Name ... EndState` block replace matching
  members inside that existing skeleton state. An unmatched member is appended
  inside the state; the patch state declaration itself is never copied.
- A line `; @state-rename oldName newName` renames exactly one state declaration
  in the skeleton and exact `GoToState("oldName")` string targets. The merge fails
  if the source state is missing/ambiguous or the destination already exists.

So you never re-declare the properties or the `Extends` line — the decompiled
skeleton keeps them; you provide the logic.

## Rules

- **No game Papyrus.** Files here MUST be original code. Never paste Bethesda's
  decompiled sources — the toolkit must not redistribute game scripts. A patch is
  just the `Event`/`Function` blocks; it is not a whole script.
- **Keyed by the script's namespaced path.** `WindChimesActivatorScript` →
  `WindChimesActivatorScript.psc`; `Fragments:Quests:Foo` →
  `Fragments/Quests/Foo.psc`. Matching is case-insensitive.
- **Reference the bound properties directly.** The property names/types come from
  the object's `VirtualMachineAdapter` (VMAD) and survive in the decompiled
  skeleton — read `mods/<Mod>/Scripts/Source/User/<name>.psc` to see them, then
  reference them in your event body (no re-declaration).
- **Mind the default state.** Appended members land in the script's empty
  (default) state. If activation must fire while the object is in a named state,
  put the event in a matching patch `State` block.
- **State blocks are structural instructions, not declarations.** They must name
  a state already supplied by the decompiled skeleton (or its name before an
  `@state-rename`). Properties, variables, `Scriptname`, and new state
  declarations still do not belong in patch files.

## Finding the gaps

Every hollow FO76 script with no patch is logged during conversion as a
`[Scripts] … decompiled with no logic (FO76 server-side stub)` warning. Read the
decompiled skeleton for its signature, then hand-write the method fill — or ask an
AI to generate one for the easy cases (give-item, cast-spell, play-sound,
enable/disable). Reconvert to pick it up.

## Upgrade-mode invalidation

Patches are applied by the `convert_scripts` phase. When the target version in
`bacup/py_bacup_lib/python/bacup_lib/resources/conversion/upgrade_manifest.yaml`
(packaged as `bacup_lib/resources/conversion/upgrade_manifest.yaml`) lists the
`Scripts` family, upgrade
mode runs that family every time, including when the installed version already
matches the target. Keep `Scripts` on the target version while iterating on this
folder; no digest refresh or version bump is required for patch edits.
